Jamison Brereton

30 (384)
Indra
Babhru ─Аtreya
15 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This hymn follows a fairly straightforward chronological trajectory. The poet begins by wondering where Indra is (vs. 1), locates him on the way to the sacrifice (vs. 2), and promises the god to recite his deeds at the ceremony (vs. 3). This recital occupies the middle of the hymn (vss. 4тАУ10), ending (vs. 11) with a return to the ritual setting, where Indra, pleased by the soma, bestows cows. This mythic model provides a smooth transition to the last four verses (12тАУ15), the poetтАЩs d─Бnastuti, praising his patrons the Ru┼Ыamas and their king, R╠ес╣Зaс╣Гcaya (lit., тАЬhe who requites his debtsтАЭ), for their gift to him of four thousand cows, plus a piece of ritual equip ment, a pot. The poet names himself in verse 14. The recital of IndraтАЩs deeds touches on the Vala myth (vs. 4), the Vr╠еtra myth (vss. 5тАУ6), and the defeat of Namuci (vss. 7тАУ8). The intriguing mention of the D─Бsa тАЬwho made women his weaponsтАЭ (vs. 9) is unfortunately more opaque; however, it may be connected with an equally opaque verse, I.104.3. In our view both passages refer to rivers controlled by the ─АryaтАЩs consistent, and perhaps indigenous, opponents, thus serving as a barrier to ─Аrya progress. The words тАЬriverтАЭ and тАЬstreamтАЭ (dh├йn─Б) are feminine in gender, and so these are the female тАЬweaponsтАЭ of 9a. Once Indra has recognized that the тАЬweaponsтАЭ are mere (female) streams, he leads the charge against the D─Бsa foe. The cows captured in this raid may be referred to in verse 10, the same cows that Indra distributes in verse 11.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra There are a number of paired repetitions of words and phrases in earlier and later parts of the hymn, but not enough to define an omphalos: e.g., -senaс╕е# 3d / s├йn─Бс╕е# 9b; X Y cakrс╣г╠е e 4a / X Y cakre 9a; yudh├бye 4b / 9d; ├б┼Ыm─Бnam cid 4c / 8c; g├бv─Бm … usr├нy─Бn─Бm 4d / 11d.

рд╡рдЬреНрд░реА рд╡рдЬреНрд░рд╡рд╛рдиреН рдкреБрд░реБрд╣реВрддрдГ рдмрд╣реБрднрд┐рд░рд╛рд╣реВрддрдГ рдпрдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рд░рд╛рдпрд╛ рджреЗрдпреЗрди рдзрдиреЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕реБрддрд╕реЛрдордорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реБрддрд╕реЛрдордВ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдордиреНрд╡рд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рдКрддреА рдКрддреНрдпреИ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдпреИ рддрддреН рддрд╕реНрдп рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рдУрдХрдГ рдЧреГрд╣рдВ рдЧрдиреНрддрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рд╡реАрд░рдГ рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реНрдпрдГ рд╕ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдХреНрд╡ рдХреБрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╕реБрдЦрд░рдердВ рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛рдХреНрд╖рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рдГ рд░рдереЛ рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕ рд╕реБрдЦрд░рдердГ ред рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рдЦрдирддрд┐ рд▓рд┐рдЦрддрд┐ рднреВрдорд┐рдорд┐рддрд┐ рд╡рд╛ рд╕реБрдЦрдореН ред рддрд╛рджреГрдЧреНрд░рдердореН ред тАШрд╕реБрд╣рд┐рддрдВ рдЦреЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдЦрдВ рдкреБрдирдГ рдЦрдирддреЗрдГ ’ ( рдирд┐рд░реБ. рей. резрей ) рдЗрддрд┐ рдпрд╛рд╕реНрдХрдГ ред рд╣рд░рд┐рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╡рд╛рд╣рдирд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдореН рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдореН рдИрдпрдорд╛рдирдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдореН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рдХреЛрд╜рдкрд╢реНрдпрддреН рдХрд╢реНрдЪ рджрджреГрд╢реЗ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhere is that hero? who has seen Indra seated in his easy chariot travelling with his horses, the thunder, the invoked of many, who, desirous of the libation is proceeding with riches to the habitation (of his worshipper) for his preservation?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Where is this hero? Who has seen Indra of the well-naved chariot speeding with his two fallow bays,
the mace-bearer, who, seeking one who has pressed the soma, will come to that home, when he is much invoked, with wealth, with help?

Jamison Brereton Notes

Despite the distance between them and the syntagms in between, I take r─Бy─Б╠Б and ┼лt─л╠Бas parallel polarized instr. to be construed primarily with g├бnt─Б. Geldner and Witzel Got┼Н differently, though also differently from each other.

It is tempting to interpr g├бnt─Б in d as a periphrastic future, a temptation yielded to in the published translation

WHERE is that Hero? Who hath looked on Indra borne on light-rolling car by Tawny Coursers,
Who, Thunderer, seeks with wealth the Soma-presser, and to his house goes, much-invoked, to aid him?

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI have looked down upon the secret and fearful plural ce of his abiding; I have repaired, desiring him, (to the plural ce of) the self-sustainer; I have inquired (of him) from others; they, the leaders (of rites), the search after wisdom, have said to me, let us have recourse to Indra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I spotted his track in secret; I followed the powerful track of the one who laid it down, seeking him.
I asked the others, and they said to me, тАЬWe men might attain Indra, since we have wakened (early).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Witzel Got┼Н take sasv├бr as тАШin sleepтАЩ, against the standard interpr. тАШin secretтАЩ, arguing that the latter does not make sense with bubudh─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е in d. But p─Бda d is not directly associated with p─Бda a, which, with b, compares the poetтАЩs pursuit of Indra to the stealthy tracking behavior of a hunter. Moreover, the other three exx. of sasv├бr(t─Б) (in a tight knot in VII.58.5, 59.7, 60.10) clearly mean тАШin secretтАЩ, as opposed to тАШin the openтАЩ (cf. the contrast in VII.58.5 with ─Бv├нr тАШopenlyтАЩ). It is true that the standard etymology of sasv├бr takes it from тИЪsas тАШsleepтАЩ (see EWA s.v. SAS), but the semantic development to тАШin secretтАЩ isnтАЩt difficult to imagine – esp. if Skt. тИЪsas, which violates standard root structure constraints, was onomatopoetic for the shushing/hushing verbal gesture (English тАЬshh,тАЭ etc.). From тАЬkeep quietтАЭ to тАЬkeep secretтАЭ is a short step. Although тИЪsas is clearly an inherited root, with cognates in Avestan and Anatolian, the onomatopoetic interpr. could be regularly (re-)actualized by association with the (near-universal?) living тАЬshhтАЭ interjection.

The position of any─Б╠Бn in b should, by my rules, make it definite (тАЬthe othersтАЭ).

Though both Geldner and Witzel Got┼Н render it as indefinite, there is no reason why it canтАЩt be definite: the poet consults with his priestly/poetic colleagues or with those тАЬwho knowтАЭ (vidv├бс╣Гs-) Their answer, referring to тАЬwe men,тАЭ suggests that it is a defined group, quite possibly the priests performing the morning ritual. The action that qualifies them for attaining Indra – waking up (early) – is surely not simply reflecting a general sentiment like тАЬthe early bird gets the worm,тАЭ but refers to IndraтАЩs attendance at the morning pressing; cf., e.g., IV.35.7 pr─Бt├бс╕е sut├бm apibo harya┼Ыva тАЬEarly in the morning you drank the pressed (soma), you of the fallow bays.тАЭ

I asked of others, and they said in answer, May we, awakened men, attain to Indra.

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреЗ рддреНрд╡рджреАрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рдпрд╛рдирд┐ рдХреГрддрд╛рдирд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рдиреБ рдЕрджреНрдп рд╡рдпрдВ рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛рд░рдГ рд╕реБрддреЗ рд╕реЛрдореЗрд╜рднрд┐рд╖реБрддреЗ рд╕рддрд┐ рддрд╛рдирд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рдкреНрд░ рдмреНрд░рд╡рд╛рдо рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖реЗрдг рд╡рджрд╛рдо ред рддреНрд╡рдордкрд┐ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорджрд░реНрдердВ рдпрд╛рдирд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рдЬреБрдЬреЛрд╖рдГ рдЕрд╕реЗрд╡рдерд╛рдГ рддрд╛рдирд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рдЕрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЗрддрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдордЬрд╛рдирдиреН рдЬрдирдГ рд╡реЗрджрддреН рдЬрд╛рдирд╛рддреБ ред рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╢реГрдгрд╡рдЪреНрдЪ рд╢реГрдгреБрдпрд╛рдЪреНрдЪ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЬрд╛рдирдиреН рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдГ рд╢реГрдгрд╡рдЪреНрдЪ ред рдЕрдЬрд╛рдирдиреНрддрдордкрд┐ рдЬрдирдВ рд╢реНрд░рд╛рд╡рдпреЗрдЪреНрдЪ ред рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реЗрдирдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рднрд┐рдГ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрдпреБрдХреНрддрдГ рдордШрд╡рд╛ рдзрдирд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЬрд╛рдирдиреН рдЕрдпрдореН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░реЛ рдЬрд╛рдирддрд╢реНрдЪ рд╢реГрдгреНрд╡рддрд╢реНрдЪ рддрд╛рдиреН рдЬрдирд╛рдиреН рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рд╡рд╣рддреЗ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реИрд░реБрд╣реНрдпрддреЗ рее рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди рдХрд░реНрддреГрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ рее рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the libation is offered, Indra, we celebrate your exploits; those (exploits) which you have been praised (to achieve) for us; let him who is ignorant acquire knowledge (of them); let him who is acquainted (with them) make them known; this Maghavan (is) the lord of hosts.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

We shall now proclaim at the pressing the deeds that are yours, Indra, which you will enjoy (hearing) from us.
He will learn who does not know, and he will hear who does know: тАЬThis bounteous one is traveling here fully armed.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

The syntax in the first hemistich is a little rough. y─Б╠Бte kс╣Ыt─Б╠Бni in p─Бda a appears to be an embedded relative clause, a construction that is rare to non-existent in the RV. Its position between the preverb and the verb of the main cl. (pr├б тАж br├бv─Бma) makes it difficult to interpret it any other way. The fact that it is a nominal clause, an NP serving as direct object, may make the embedding seem less of a syntactic violation. (Note that Geldner simply ignores the rel. prn.) The main verb br├бv─Бma is accented because it is effectively in p─Бda-initial position: the initial accented voc. ├нndra is extra-clausal.

The second rel. clause y─Б╠Бni no j├║joс╣гaс╕е тАЬwhich of ours you will enjoyтАЭ appears to be parallel to the embedded NP, but it is a little skewed semantically. Indra should not enjoy his deeds, but rather enjoy hearing our recital of them (see Geldner тАЬdie du von uns gern h├╢ren wirstтАЭ [my italics], with тАШhearтАЩ silently supplied). Alternatively it would be possible to assume that the 2nd rel. is (covertly) conjoined to the first and refers to different deeds, тАЬ(and) which (deeds) of ours you will enjoyтАЭ – but it is hardly likely that Indra cares about what we do (besides pressing soma), so this interpr. is pragmatically blocked. Witzel Got┼Н supply тАЬ(in) unseren (Worten)тАЭ as the antecedent to the second rel. prn., such that what Indra will enjoy is our words, not his deeds (тАЬ(in) unseren (Worten), an welchen du Freude hastтАЭ); this seems to me to deploy too much machinery to repair what is simply a somewhat loose expression.

It would be technically possible to take the first hemistich as consisting only of relative clauses, with the main clause represented by c with an unexpressed resumptive тАЬ(those deeds)тАЭ: тАЬWhich deeds of yours we shall now proclaim at the pressing, which you will enjoy, (those deeds) he will learn …тАЭ The accent on br├бv─Бma would then be because it is in a dependent clause. Although this interpr.

would save us from an embedded relative (see above), the rhetoric of the 1st hemistich, with pr├б n├║ vay├бm тАж br├бv─Бma reminiscent of I.32.1 ├нndrasya n├║ v─лry─Б╠Ас╣Зi pr├б vocam and similar passages, strongly suggests an annunciatory declaration rather than a subordination.

Griffith

We will tell, Indra, when we pour libation, what mighty deeds thou hast performed to please us.
Let him who knows not learn, who knows them listen: hither rides Maghavan with all his army.

Geldner

Nun wollen wir bei Soma deine Taten verk├╝nden, o Indra, die du von uns gern h├╢ren wirst. Es soll sie der Unkundige kennen lernen und der Kundige soll zuh├╢ren: Da f├дhrt der Gabenreiche in voller Wehr!

Grassmann

So wolln wir, Indra, deine Thaten preisen bei diesem Safte, was von uns du gern hast, Wer nicht weiss, wisse, wer es weiss, vernehme: ┬╗Mit ganzer Heerschar f├дhret dieser m├дcht’ge.┬л

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAs soon as genitive rated, Indra, you have made your mind resolved; you have gone alone to contend against numerous (foes); you have rent asunder the rock by your strength; you have rescued the herd of milk-yielding kine.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You made your mind steadfast when you were just born, Indra; even alone you pursue the many for battle.
You made even a stone flash like lightning through your vast power; you found the pen of the ruddy cows.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) assume that c, like d, refers to the opening of the Vala cave. They therefore either take didyuto v├н тАШflashed forthтАЩ as a stand in for тАШbroke/split apartтАЩ (Geldner, flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs vyabhinaс╕е) or disjoin didyutaс╕е from v├н and supply another verb with the preverb (or so I understand Witzel Got┼НтАЩs тАЬтАж blitzend, zer(sprengt)тАЭ). But c and d do not have to refer to a single feat: a and b do not, and the recital of kс╣Ыt─Б╠Бni promised in 3ab covers a number of different deeds in the vss. to come. Moreover, though ├б┼Ыman- тАШstoneтАЩ can refer to the Vala cave, it has a number of other possible referents (see 8c where NamuciтАЩs head is equated/compared with an ├б┼Ыman-), including IndraтАЩs own weapon. Cf. IV.22.1 y├│ ├б┼Ыm─Бnaс╣Г ┼Ы├бvas─Б b├нbhrad ├йti тАЬwho [=Indra] keeps bearing the stone with his power,тАЭ with the ┼Ы├бvas─Б found also here. Since тИЪdyut is very commonly found with v├н (including the common and lexicalized root-noun cmpd.

vidy├║t- тАШlightningтАЩ) and since one of the sites to which a preverb in tmesis moves is directly after its verb (and here also adjoining a metrical boundary), it seems very likely that preverb and verb belong together – and have their normal sense. In my interpr. this lexeme incorporates a simile: тАШcause to flash like lightningтАЩ / тАШcause to lightningтАЩ (unfortunately English does not have such a verb). In other words, with his power Indra can make even the dull and homely material stone flash like a lightning bolt.

Griffith

Indra, when born, thou madest firm thy spirit: alone thou seekest war to fight with many.
With might thou clavest e’en the rock asunder, and foundest out the stable of the Milch-kine.

Geldner

Sobald du geboren wurdest, hast du deinen Sinn gest├дhlt, o Indra. Du verlangst ganz allein sogar eine ├Ьberzahl zu bek├дmpfen. Auch die Felsh├╢hle hast du mit Gewalt erbrochen; du fandest die H├╢hle der r├╢tlichen K├╝he.

Grassmann

Geboren machtest deinen Sinn du stark schon, auch viele greifst allein du an zum Kampfe; Den Fels auch blitztest kr├дftig fort du, Indra, errangst den Stall der morgenrothen K├╝he.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen you have been born most excellent and supreme, bearing a name widely renowned, then the gods have been in dread of Indra, and he has subjugated all the waters, the brides of the slave (Vс╣Ыtra).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When you were born far away in the farthest (realm), bearing a name famous afar,
from then on even the gods feared Indra. He conquered all the waters, those whose husband [=Vr╠еtra] was a D─Бsa.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The Pp. interprets param├б as nom. sg. m. param├бс╕е, and Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) follow suit. I prefer the equally possible reading param├й, on the basis of several тАШbornтАЩ passages with this expression. Cf., e.g., I.143.2 s├б j─Б╠Бyam─Бnaс╕е param├й vy├▓man (though the subj. is Agni there).

In my view cid often takes WackernagelтАЩs Law position, even when it seems to limit a different word in the clause. Hence my тАЬeven the gods,тАЭ though dev─Б╠Б(с╕е) is at the end of the p─Бda. Its positioning there may be to take advantage of its adjacency to v├н┼Ыv─Б(с╕е) across the p─Бda boundary. Although the latter is fem. and must modify acc. pl. ap├бс╕е тАШwatersтАЩ, its position evokes the common locution тАЬall the gods / the All Gods.тАЭ In fact, the expression тАЬall the watersтАЭ is vanishingly rare тАФ besides this passage I have found only VII.95.1 тАФ and so тАЬallтАЭ belongs more naturally with the immediately preceding тАЬgodsтАЭ than with its grammatical partner.

Note the switch from 2nd ps. ref. to Indra (rel. cl. 5ab) to 3rd ps. ref. (main cl.

5c, new cl. 5d).

Griffith

When thou wast born supremest at a distance, bearing a name renowned in far-off regions,
Since then e’en Gods have been afraid of Indra: he conquered all the floods which served the Dasa.

Als du, der weitaus H├╢chste, geboren wurdest, deinen r├╝hmlichen Namen in die Ferne tragend, von da ab f├╝rchteten sich auch die G├╢tter vor Indra. Alle Gew├дsser eroberte er, deren Herr Gemahl der Dasa war.

Grassmann

Als du als h├╢chster ferneher erschienest, weithin verbreitend den ber├╝hmten Namen, Da f├╝rchteten vor Indra sich die G├╢tter, die feindbeherrschten Wasser all errang er.

рдПрддреЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ ред рдорд╣рджреНрд░рд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рд╡рджрдиреНрддреАрддрд┐’ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛рд░рдГред рд╕реБрд╢реЗрд╡рд╛рдГ ред рд╢реЗрд╡рдорд┐рддрд┐ рд╕реБрдЦрдирд╛рдореИрддрддреН ред рд╢реЛрднрдирд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрдГ ред рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░реЗрдг рд╢реЛрднрдирдВ рд╕реБрдЦрдореБрддреНрдкрд╛рджрдпрдиреНрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреБрднреНрдпреЗрддреН рддреБрднреНрдпрдореЗрд╡ рдЕрд░реНрдХрдореН рдЕрд░реНрдЪрдиреАрдпрдВ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рдореН рдЕрд░реНрдЪрдиреНрддрд┐ рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЕрдиреНрдзрдГ рд╕реЛрдорд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдордиреНрдирдВ ‘рд╕реБрдиреНрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рдЕрднрд┐рд╖рд╡рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрддрдГ ‘рдорд╛рдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдЕрд╣рд┐рдВ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рдВ рдкреНрд░ рд╕рдХреНрд╖рддреН рдЕрднреНрдпрднрд╡рддреН ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдореН ред рдУрд╣рд╛рдирдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдмрд╛рдзрдорд╛рдирдореН рдЕрдкрдГ рдЙрджрдХрд╛рдирд┐ рдЖрд╢рдпрд╛рдирдореН рдЖрд╡реГрддреНрдп рд╢рдпрдирдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рдорд╛рдпрд┐рдирдВ рдХрдкрдЯрд╡рдиреНрддрдорд┐рддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese devoted Maruts eulogise you with pious praise, and pour out to you the sacrificial food; Indra has overcome by his device the guileful Ahi, harassing the gods and arresting the waters.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Maruts: Or, maruts may here signify praisers, worshippers, stot─Бraс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Just for you do these friendly Maruts chant the chant, press the stalk. The serpent vaunting himself, lying on the watersтАФIndra will overcome the tricky one with tricks.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Referent shift continues: 2nd ps. in ab, 3rd in cd.

Griffith

These blissful Maruts sing their psalm to praise thee, and pour to thee libation of the Soma.
Indra with wondrous powers subdued the Dragon, the guileful lurker who beset the waters.

Dir, dir ja singen alle diese Maruts, die holden, Loblied, keltern Somakr├дuter, Ihn, welcher lauernd um die Wasser dalag, den list’gen Drachen schlug mit Listen Indra.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рддреБрднреНрдп) рддреБрднреНрдпрдореНред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рднрдХреНрддреЗрд░реНрд▓реБрдХреН (рдЗрддреН) рдПрд╡ (рдПрддреЗ) (рдорд░реБрддрдГ) рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрдГ (рд╕реБрд╢реЗрд╡рд╛рдГ) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдГ (рдЕрд░реНрдЪрдиреНрддрд┐) рд╕рддреНрдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ (рдЕрд░реНрдХрдореН) рд╕рддреНрдХрд░рдгреАрдпрдореН (рд╕реБрдиреНрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐) рдирд┐рд╖реНрдкрд╛рджрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ (рдЕрдиреНрдзрдГ) рдЕрдиреНрдирдореН (рдЕрд╣рд┐рдореН) рдореЗрдШрдореН (рдУрд╣рд╛рдирдореН) рддреНрдпрдЬрдиреНрддрдореН (рдЕрдкрдГ) рдЬрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ (рдЖрд╢рдпрд╛рдирдореН) рдпрдГ рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рдЪреНрдЫреЗрддреЗ рддрдореН (рдкреНрд░) (рдорд╛рдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рднрд┐рдГ (рдорд╛рдпрд┐рдирдореН) рдХреБрддреНрд╕рд┐рддрд╛ рдорд╛рдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрддреЗ рдпрд╕реНрдп рддрдореН (рд╕рдХреНрд╖рддреН) рд╕рдорд╡реИрддрд┐ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрддреН рееремрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaghavan, who are glorified by us, assailing with the thunderbolt the antagonist (of the gods), you have slain those who were ever hostile (to you) from your birth; desiring to do good to Manu, you have bruised the head of the slave Namuci.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Desiring to do good to Manu: manave g─Бtum icchan: g─Бtum = sukham; identifying Manu with the с╣Ыс╣гi of the s┼лkta, namucina ap─Бhс╣Ыtagodhan─Бya mahyam, to me whose wealth of cattle has been carried off by Namuci, an asura

Jamison Brereton

You hewed apart those negligent by nature, stimulating giving, o bounteous one, taking pleasure along with the cow,
at the time when you caused the head of the D─Бsa Namuci to roll,
seeking an (open) way for ManuтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

There are several uncertainties in this vs. As often the function and syntactic affiliation of jan├║с╣г─Б are unclear. I construe it with mс╣Ы╠Бdhaс╕е, but Geldner and Witzel Got┼Н (in different ways) take it with Indra. This is also possible.

The participial phrase d─Б╠Бnam ├нnvan тАЬstimulating givingтАЭ seems oddly embedded in the distracted VP v├н с╣г├║ mс╣Ы╠Бdhaс╕е тАж ├бhan тАЬyou hewed apart the negligent ones.тАЭ The positioning between the preverb and its verb in tmesis may be a kind of iconic reflection of the separation sense of the preverb (тАШapartтАЩ). For a similar ex. see I.103.2. On the participial phrase see further below.

I have been puzzled by the phrase g├бv─Б тАж saс╣Гcak─Бn├бс╕е, though I think I now see a solution (see below). For one thing, тИЪk─Б [/kan] is not otherwise found with s├бm (anywhere in Sanskrit, at least judging from Monier-Williams); for another, this root is not construed with the instr. (pace Grassmann, whose supposed exx. should all be interpr.

otherwise). And finally I cannot think of a (solitary) cow that figures prominently in Indra mythology, either as a companion (as I took it in the published translation) or as a source of enjoyment. Geldner remarks (n. 7a) that Indra gives abundantly as long as he is тАЬim Genuss der erbeuteten K├╝he.тАЭ I suppose this is possible but it assumes a fairly extensive backstory. Like me, K├╝mmel (143) takes the cow as comitative: тАЬmit Rindvieh тАж dich zusammenw├╝nschend.тАЭ I was happy to have company in this tr., but I frankly didnтАЩt understand what either his or mine is actually meant to express. Witzel Got┼Н also seem to have a comitative reading, which is similarly opaque: тАЬdu erpicht darauf wirst, mit dem Rind beisammen zu sein.тАЭ On reconsideration of the passage I now see a possible solution. It is striking that g├бv─Б is the only apparent occurrence of the instr. sg. to this stem in the RV. In context it appears directly before maghavan. I now think the original form may have been gen. pl. *g├бv─Бm, with simplification of the double -m m-. The meter is unaffected, and a gen. pl. would fit the sense much better, as I will now show. This hymn contains four other examples of this very gen. pl. (4d, 11d, 12b, 13b), as well as nom. pl. g─Б╠Бvaс╕е (10a). The examples in 12 and 13 are in a d─Бnastuti, but the others refer to the cows that Indra freed from the Vala cave (and are in the same metrical position as our form). I see two possible ways to construe my putative *g├бv─Бm. Since forms of тИЪk─Б can take the genitive as a source of enjoyment (e.g., X.54.16 dr├бviс╣Зasaс╕е), it may go with saс╣Гcak─Бn├бс╕е: тАЬenjoying the cows,тАЭ referring to IndraтАЩs pleasure in his deed and its products. But in vs. 11 Indra, having drunk soma, p├║nar g├бv─Бm adad─Бd usr├нy─Бс╣З─Бm тАЬgave again of the ruddy cows.тАЭ This seems to refer to a redistribution on the ritual ground of the cows that Indra had freed. Bringing together 11d g├бv─Бm adad─Бt with 7ab d─Б╠Бnam ├нnvan тАж *g├бv─Бm, I am inclined to think that the cows are the content of the gift and would now alter the tr. to тАЬsetting in motion the gift *of cowsтАЭ vel sim. Under this interpr. saс╣Гcak─Бn├бс╕е is used without complement: тАЬtaking pleasure, enjoying yourselfтАЭ (for a similar absolute use of this participle, see IV.16.15 and K├╝mmel 143). Thus the hemistich contains a brief pr├йcis of the myth: Indra hews apart those who block his freeing of the cows [I would now probably change my rendering of mс╣Ы╠е╠Бdhaс╕е as тАШnegligentтАЩ here], which allows him to set in motion the ultimate giving away of the freed cows, and he thoroughly (s├бm) enjoys the whole process. The occurrences of g├бv─Бm in the d─Бnastuti (esp. 12b g├бv─Бс╣Г catv─Б╠Бri d├бdataс╕е sah├бsr─Б) simply replicate the mythic model provided by IndraтАЩs generous sharing out of the freed cows.

I am not certain what p─Бda d is conveying. How is it that IndraтАЩs setting NamuciтАЩs head to rolling involves тАЬseeking a way for ManuтАЭ? Unfortunately we can glean too little about Namuci from the RV (where he is mentioned only 9x) to know what threat he posed that required Indra to kill him. On the other hand, judging from the usual troubles caused by D─Бsas and, particularly, from vs. 9 (see published introduction.), these foes stand in the way of ─Аrya movement into new territory. Thus Indra by eliminating Namuci would open the way for Manu and the rest of the advancing ─Аrya.

Griffith

Thou, Maghavan, from the first didst scatter foemen, speeding, while joying in the milk, the Giver.
There, seeking man’s prosperity, thou torest away the head of Namuci the Dasa.

Geldner

Du zersprengtest gleich bei deiner Geburt die Ver├дchter v├╢llig, der Freigebigkeit ihren Lauf lassend, wenn du dich der Kuh erfreust, o Gabenreicher. Das war damals als du das Haupt des Dasa Namuci ins Rollen brachtest, f├╝r Manu die freie Bahn suchend.

Grassmann

Nach deiner Art zerschlugst du bald die Feinde, durch Trank erfrischt, die Gabe f├╢rdernd, starker, Als dort das Haupt des Namutschi, des D├дmons, du rollen liessest, Heil dem Menschen wirkend.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реЗрдг рд╕рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдирдВ рднреНрд░рдордиреНрддрдореН рдЕрд╢реНрдорд╛рдирдВ рдЪрд┐рддреН рдореЗрдШрдорд┐рд╡ рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрдВ рджрд╛рд╕рд╕реНрдп рдЙрдкрдХреНрд╖рдкрдпрд┐рддреБрдГ рдирдореБрдЪреЗрдГ рдЕрд╕реБрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╢рд┐рд░рдГ рдордерд╛рдпрдиреН рдЪреВрд░реНрдгрдпрдиреН рдЖрджрд┐рддреН рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░рдореЗрд╡ рдорд╛рдВ рдпреБрдЬрдВ рд╕рдЦрд╛рдпрдореН рдЕрдХреГрдерд╛рдГ рд╣рд┐ рдЪрдХреГрд╖реЗ рдЦрд▓реБ ред рддрджрд╛рдиреАрдВ рдорд░реБрджреНрдзрдпрдГ рддреНрд╡рддреНрд╕рд╣рд╛рдпреЗрднреНрдпрдГ рд░реЛрджрд╕реА рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ рдЪрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпреЗрд╡ рдЪрдХреНрд░реЗ рдЗрд╡ рдкреНрд░ рдЖрд╕реНрддрд╛рдореН рее рдЙрдкрд╕рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрд░реБрддреЗрд░реНрдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рд╣рд╛рд░рдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬVerily you have made me, Indra, your associate when grinding the head of the slave Namuci like a sounding and rolling cloud; and the heaven and earth (have been caused) by the Maruts (to revolve like a wheel).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like a sounding and rolling cloud: a┼Ыm─Бnam cit svaryam vartam─Бnam: the first two are rendered megham iva, like a cloud

Jamison Brereton

For you have made me your yokemate, IndraтАФjust afterward stealing the head of the D─Бsa Namuci,
which was rolling, (like?) a whizzing stone, like the two world-halves (that roll) forth like two wheels, for the Maruts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Though this vs. follows thematically on vs. 7, it seems disjointed and has given rise to much discussion (see esp. Oldenberg and his skepticism about GeldnerтАЩs interpr.; Bloomfield Rig-Veda Repetitions) and incompatible interpretations, which I will not treat in detail further here.

The first question that arises is who is the 1st

-ps. speaker in p─Бda a. Geldner suggests that it is Namuci himself, a suggestion rejected by both Oldenberg and Bloomfield I think the root aor. ├бkс╣Ыth─Бс╕е is the clue. It is rare that the aorist, esp. the root aorist, is used as a narrative tense, esp. to a root well outfitted with other preterital possibilities. I take p─Бda a as a parenthetical interruption of the Namuci story, prompted by the last p─Бda of vs. 7, esp. the mention of Manu. With Oldenberg I take тАЬmeтАЭ as referring to the present-day priest, and in my view he is asserting his ancestral and vocational connection with the primal priest and representative ─Аrya, Manu. The speaker suggests that IndraтАЩs current partnership with him (тАЬfor you have made me your yokemateтАЭ with the aorist of the recent past) is evidence of IndraтАЩs active concern for his ancestor Manu in the mythological past. After this interruption ─Б╠Бd ├нd functions as a resumptive expression, returning us to and carrying on the story of the myth narrated in 7cd.

In 8c the referent of the тАЬwhizzing stoneтАЭ (├б┼Ыm─Бnam тАж svary├аm) is disputed.

I very much doubt that it is a mountain, despite the occurrence of the same expression in V.56.4, where it definitely is a mountain, and despite OldenbergтАЩs championing of this identification. I think it more likely that the phrase resonates with I.32.2 v├бjraс╣Г svary├аm, where svary├а- refers to IndraтАЩs mace. NamuciтАЩs whirling head is being compared to a weapon whirling through the air and making a whizzing sound.

The тАЬrolling, whirlingтАЭ image is carried further in the next p─Бda, with the simile тАЬ(rolling forth) like two wheels.тАЭ The simile makes fine sense with v├бrtam─Бna-, but what are the two world-halves (r├│das─л) doing there? As it turns out, though it may seem counter-intuitive in real-world terms, the two worlds (under various designations) are regularly associated with the root тИЪvс╣Ыt (cf., e.g., V.43.2, VI.8.3, VII.80.1, VIII.6.5). In some of these passages the rolling out of the two worlds is part of a cosmogonic exercise; in some it refers to the visual (re- )appearance of differentiated earth and sky at dawn.

I have no idea what the Maruts are doing here.

Griffith

Pounding the head of Namuci the Dasa, me, too thou madest thine associate, Indra!
Yea, and the rolling stone that is in heaven both worlds, as on a car, brought to the Maruts.

Geldner

Du hast mich ja zu deinem Verb├╝ndeten gemacht" - aber du, Indra, hast das Haupt des Dasa Namuci wirbelnd ins Rollen gebracht, das wie ein sausender Fels rollte. Himmel und Erde rollten es wie R├дder den Marut zu.

Grassmann

Du machtest Indra da mich zum Genossen, das Haupt umwirbelnd Namutschi, dem D├дmon, Den Schleuderstein zugleich, der rauschend rollte, den Maruts Erd’ und Himmel wie zwei R├дder.

Elizarenkova

рджрд╛рд╕рдГ рдЙрдкрдХреНрд╖рдкрдпрд┐рддрд╛ рдирдореБрдЪрд┐рд░рд╕реБрд░рдГ рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдпрдГ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА: рдЖрдпреБрдзрд╛рдирд┐ рдпреБрджреНрдзрд╕рд╛рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдЪрдХреНрд░реЗ рд╣рд┐ рдХреГрддрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЦрд▓реБ ред рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░реЗрдг рд╕рд╣ рдпреЛрджреНрдзреБрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╣рд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдЕрд╕реБрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдиреНрдпрдГ рдЕрдмрд▓рд╛рдГ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрд░реВрдкрд╛рдГ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдГ рдорд╛ рдорд╛рдВ рдХрд┐рдВ рдХрд░рдиреН ред рдХрд┐рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпреБрд░рд┐рддрд┐ рдордиреНрдпрдорд╛рди рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рд╕рд╛рдВ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдЕрд╕реБрд░рд╕реНрдп рдзреЗрдиреЗ рдкреНрд░реАрдгрдпрд┐рддреНрд░реНрдпреМ рд╕реБрд░реВрдкреЗ рдЙрднреЗ рджреНрд╡реЗ рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдпреМ рдЕрдиреНрддрдГ рдЕрдЦреНрдпрддреН рд╣рд┐ рдЧреГрд╣рдордзреНрдпреЗ рдирд┐рджрдзреЗ рдЦрд▓реБ ред рдЕрде рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░рдореН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рджрд╕реНрдпреБрдВ рдирдореБрдЪрд┐рдВ рдпреБрдзрдпреЗ рдпреБрджреНрдзрд╛рдп рдЙрдк рдкреНрд░реИрддреН рдЙрдкрдкреНрд░рд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe slave (Namuci) made women his weapons what will his feminine le hosts do unto me? The two his best beloved, (Indra) confined in the inner apartments, and then went forth to combat against the Dasyus.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

What will his feminine le hosts do unto me? Indra is supposed to say this; the two his best beloved: decapitation of Namuci by Indra is related in the gad─Б section of the ┼Ъalya parva of the Mah─Бbh─Бrata; Namuci through fear of Indra, took refuge in the solar rays; Indra promised that he would not harm him if he came forth, but broke his promise, and, on Namuci’s issuing forth, cut off his head; by this he incurred the guilt of brahmanicide, for, Namuci was a brahman, but Indra was taught expiation of his sin by Brahm─Б

Jamison Brereton

Because the D─Бsa made women his weapons, what can they do to me? His armies lack strength.694 V.31
Since he [=Indra] distinguished both his [=the D─БsaтАЩs?] streams,
therefore Indra advanced on the Dasyu to fight.

Jamison Brereton Notes

For women as weapons see not only I.104.3 mentioned in the published introduction. but also X.27.10 and disc. ad loc. For my interpretation of the sense of this vs., see published introduction. I am tolerably certain about my reading of the first hemistich, but p─Бda c is more challenging and has given rise to some curious interpretations. Geldner tr. тАЬdenn er hatte darunter seine zwei Frauenbr├╝ste entdeckt,тАЭ commenting (perplexingly, at least to me) тАЬDie beiden Milchbr├╝ste f├╝r seine beiden FrauenтАЭ (n. 9c). (One would assume there would be four in all, at any rate.) Oldenberg thinks the two dh├йne refer to the two liquids in the Namuci myth and ultimately (see his ref. to his own NGGW 1893 art. [=KlSch.

635ff.]) to the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л ritual and its two separate oblations, milk and sur─Б.

Schmidt (Ged. Nyberg), more or less flg. Bloomfield, suggests that Indra recognizes two streams within himself, songs and libations, but this linkage of the literal and metaphorical through an elliptical dual seems quite unlikely. Witzel Got┼НтАЩs тАЬDarunter aber hat er dessen beide Str├╢me erblicktтАЭ is literally close to mine, but they provide no guidance on what they mean by тАЬhis two streams.тАЭ My own tr. (тАЬdistinguished both his [=D─БsaтАЩs?] streamsтАЭ) is also not as informative as it might be. One problem is the meaning of the lexeme ant├бr тИЪkhy─Б.

To тИЪkhy─Б тАШseeтАЩ ant├бr should add the sense of either тАШlook withinтАЩ or тАШdistinguish betweenтАЩ. The similarly formed ant├бr тИЪpa┼Ы seems to have both these meanings: тАШlook withinтАЩ in I.132.3 and тАШdistinguish betweenтАЩ in II.27.3. (In the latter passage JPB tr.

тАШlook withinтАЩ, but I consider that the less likely sense in context.) In the only other occurrence of ant├бr тИЪkhy─Б, I.81.9, I tr. тАШdetectтАЩ (flg. GeldnerтАЩs тАШendeckenтАЩ for this passage, V.30.9), a sense that can be somewhat tenuously derived from тАШlook within a mass of stuff тАФ and visually locateтАЩ. ItтАЩs also possible in that passage, which concerns the possessions of the impious, which Indra is supposed to bring to us, that he is distinguishing between those possessions and the ones that belong to deserving people and should stay put. In our passage here we might in the first instance think that тАШdistinguish betweenтАЩ would be a promising candidate, given the dual object. But I donтАЩt think Indra is supposed to be seeing a difference between the two streams, but rather perceiving that they are just streams and therefore not formidable weapons – thus encouraging his advance to fighting in p─Бda d. I am tempted to emend the published

tr. to тАЬdetected/recognized both of his (weapons) as (just) streams.тАЭ Though the weapons (─Б╠Бyudh─Бni) were plural in p─Бda a, I think that is a general statement about turning women into weapons, whereas p─Бda c concerns the particular situation Indra confronts, the two barrier rivers – the same situation as in I.104.3, which also contains two troublesome rivers.

V.30.12, 14: The Anukr. takes с╣Ыс╣Зaс╣Гcay├б- as the PN of the king, and the standard interpr. follow this, incl. the published translation I now wonder if it is at least a speaking name - and perhaps not a name at all but a descriptor: тАЬrequiting debts.тАЭ The royal patron who distributes largesse to poets and priests at a sacrifice is, from the point of view of the ritual economy, requiting his debts to them, who attracted the gods to the sacrifice and entertained them, leading them to grant tangible and intangible rewards to the patron.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the cows were separated from their calves, they wandered about hither and thither; but when the well-offered libations had exhilarated hi, then Indra, with his vigorous (maruts), reunited them (with their calves).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Together the cows then lowed on every side, since they were here, there, and everywhere separated from their calves.
Along with his powerful (men) Indra drove them together, when the well-pressed soma drinks exhilarated him.

Griffith

Divided from their calves the Cows went lowing around, on every side, hither and thither.
These Indra re-united with his helpers, what time the well-pressed Soma made him joyful.

Geldner

Grassmann

Da br├╝llten rings die K├╝he hier und dorten, weil sie getrennt von ihren K├дlbern waren; Sie all entliess durch seine Helfer Indra, als ihn berauscht die sch├╢ngebrauten Tr├дnke.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the libations effused by Babhru had exhilarated him, the showerer (of benefits) shouted aloud in the combats; Indra, the destroyer fo cities, quaffing (the Soma), restored to him his milk-yielding cattle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When the soma drinks rinsed by Babhru exhilarated him, the bull set up a bellowing among the (ritual) seats.
The stronghold-splitting Indra, having drunk of it, gave again of the ruddy cows.

Griffith

What time the Somas mixed by Babhru cheered him, loud the Steer bellowed in his habitations.
So Indra drank thereof, the Fort-destroyer, and gave him guerdon, in return, of milch-kine.

Geldner

Grassmann

Als ihn berauscht der Trank, den Babhru quirlte, da br├╝llte laut der Stier auf seinen Sitzen; Als Indra ihn getrunken, bracht’ er wieder die morgenrothen K├╝he Burgen brechend.

Elizarenkova

Jamison Brereton Notes

The two p─Бda-final sequences p├бritakmy─Бy─Бс╕е (13d) and p├бritakmy─Б y─Б╠Бm╠Р (14a) in adjacent p─Бdas are puzzling. The published translation reflects emendations of both forms to loc. sg. p├бritakmy─Бy─Бm. This loc. occurs 6x, always p─Бda-final, including in the next hymn, V.31.11 – by far the most common form to this stem. Moreover, VI.24.9d is identical to 14d, save for having the loc. p├бritakmy─Бy─Бm – a variation that Bloomfield (RVReps) finds тАЬbaffling.тАЭ The arguments in favor of emendation are the dominance of the loc. sg. and its appearance both in the next hymn and in the otherwise identical p─Бda in VI.24.9. However, these arguments cut both ways: it is difficult to understand how these forms would have become mangled - especially given the dominance of that same loc. sg. It cannot be claimed that the redactors misunderstood the forms because they had never seen their like. I therefore now feel that we must accept that the forms were in the urtext, deliberately produced by the poet, who was playing games with this well-known p─Бda-final temporal expression. I still believe that the intent of both forms is the same as the loc., but that the loc. has been deliberately altered, in two different ways, conditioned by the immediate context.

In 13d akt├│r vy├╣с╣гс╣нau p├бritakmy─Бy─Бс╕е the form has been given a genitive ending to conform, superficially, to the gen. akt├│с╕е. Grassmann takes it to an adjectival stem (p├бritakmya-, which doesnтАЩt exist) as a modifier of akt├│с╕е, which, as Oldenberg points out, would then have to be fem. here, rather than its normal masc. Oldenberg suggests it might be a gen. of time, though he prefers to supply r─Б╠Бtry─Бс╕е or to have it depend on vy├╣с╣гс╣нau.

I consider this over-thinking: the poet gives us the loc. form we expect, right up to the very last segment (-с╕е rather than -m) and then springs the surprise, capitalizing on the superficial resemblance to the gen. sg. ├бktoс╕е.

In 14a a├║chat s─Б╠Бr─Б╠Бtr─л p├бritakmy─Б y─Б╠Бm╠Рthe final syllable of the loc. has been truncated and given an accent. The anun─Бsika can be taken as hiatus-breaking nasalization of a final -─Б╠Бbefore с╣Ы; this is the standard interpr. (see esp. Oldenberg, Noten, with ref. to Prol.). This yields the nom. sg. fem. rel. prn., which allows an interpr. as a nominal rel. clause p├бritakmy─Б y─Б╠Б, which specifies immediately preceding s─Б╠Бr─Б╠Бtr─л.

A p─Бda-final rel. pronoun and the resulting nominal rel. clause (тАЬтАж the night, which is p├бritakmy─БтАЭ) would be highly unusual, but as a poetic trick involving resegmentation of a well-known form it shows a proto-┼Ыleс╣гa sensibility.

The fact that the poet alters the expected form in two different ways in succeeding p─Бdas should alert us to the fact that he is playing verbal tricks, secure in the knowledge that his audience would expect and interpret both as underlyingly locatival. For a different manipulation of the stem, see comm. ad I.31.6. In any case the published translation should have an * before тАЬat its final turnтАЭ in both instances.

English translation:

тАЬThe (gloom-) investing night has dispersed with the dawn (upon the appearance of) с╣Ъс╣Зa├▒caya, the r─Бj─Б of the ru┼Ыam─Бs; Babhru being summoned, going like a fleet courser, has received the four thousand (cattle).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(When) that night brightened at its final turn, at (the hands of)
R╠ес╣Зaс╣Гcaya, king of the Ru┼Ыamas,
like a steed quick in competition, being driven [/anointed], Babhru won four thousand (cows).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The primary reading of ajy├бm─Бnaс╕е is surely тАЬbeing driven,тАЭ as the standard interpr. have it. But it could also be the passive of тИЪa├▒j тАШanointтАЩ and inhabit the same semantic realm as тАЬwell-ornamented with thousands of cowsтАЭ in 13ab: he would be anointed with prize cows.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The two p─Бda-final sequences p├бritakmy─Бy─Бс╕е (13d) and p├бritakmy─Б y─Б╠Бm╠Р (14a) in adjacent p─Бdas are puzzling. The published translation reflects emendations of both forms to loc. sg. p├бritakmy─Бy─Бm. This loc. occurs 6x, always p─Бda-final, including in the next hymn, V.31.11 – by far the most common form to this stem. Moreover, VI.24.9d is identical to 14d, save for having the loc. p├бritakmy─Бy─Бm – a variation that Bloomfield (RVReps) finds тАЬbaffling.тАЭ The arguments in favor of emendation are the dominance of the loc. sg. and its appearance both in the next hymn and in the otherwise identical p─Бda in VI.24.9. However, these arguments cut both ways: it is difficult to understand how these forms would have become mangled - especially given the dominance of that same loc. sg. It cannot be claimed that the redactors misunderstood the forms because they had never seen their like. I therefore now feel that we must accept that the forms were in the urtext, deliberately produced by the poet, who was playing games with this well-known p─Бda-final temporal expression. I still believe that the intent of both forms is the same as the loc., but that the loc. has been deliberately altered, in two different ways, conditioned by the immediate context.

In 13d akt├│r vy├╣с╣гс╣нau p├бritakmy─Бy─Бс╕е the form has been given a genitive ending to conform, superficially, to the gen. akt├│с╕е. Grassmann takes it to an adjectival stem (p├бritakmya-, which doesnтАЩt exist) as a modifier of akt├│с╕е, which, as Oldenberg points out, would then have to be fem. here, rather than its normal masc. Oldenberg suggests it might be a gen. of time, though he prefers to supply r─Б╠Бtry─Бс╕е or to have it depend on vy├╣с╣гс╣нau.

I consider this over-thinking: the poet gives us the loc. form we expect, right up to the very last segment (-с╕е rather than -m) and then springs the surprise, capitalizing on the superficial resemblance to the gen. sg. ├бktoс╕е.

In 14a a├║chat s─Б╠Бr─Б╠Бtr─л p├бritakmy─Б y─Б╠Бm╠Рthe final syllable of the loc. has been truncated and given an accent. The anun─Бsika can be taken as hiatus-breaking nasalization of a final -─Б╠Бbefore с╣Ы; this is the standard interpr. (see esp. Oldenberg, Noten, with ref. to Prol.). This yields the nom. sg. fem. rel. prn., which allows an interpr. as a nominal rel. clause p├бritakmy─Б y─Б╠Б, which specifies immediately preceding s─Б╠Бr─Б╠Бtr─л.

A p─Бda-final rel. pronoun and the resulting nominal rel. clause (тАЬтАж the night, which is p├бritakmy─БтАЭ) would be highly unusual, but as a poetic trick involving resegmentation of a well-known form it shows a proto-┼Ыleс╣гa sensibility.

The fact that the poet alters the expected form in two different ways in succeeding p─Бdas should alert us to the fact that he is playing verbal tricks, secure in the knowledge that his audience would expect and interpret both as underlyingly locatival. For a different manipulation of the stem, see comm. ad I.31.6. In any case the published translation should have an * before тАЬat its final turnтАЭ in both instances.

Griffith

Night, well-nigh ended, at Rnancaya’s coming, King of the Rusamas, was changed to morning.
Like a strong courser, fleet of foot, urged onward, Babhru hath gained four thousand as his guerdon.

Geldner

Die Nacht, die die entscheidende war, wurde bei Riamicaya, dem K├╢nig der Rusama┬┤s hell. Wie ein siegreiches, rasches Rennpferd, wenn es zum Wettkampf getrieben wird, hat Babhru Viertausend gewonnen.

Grassmann

рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рд╡рдпрдВ рд░реБрд╢рдореЗрд╖реБ рдПрддрддреНрд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮрдХреЗрд╖реБ рдЬрдиреЗрд╖реБ рдЧрд╡реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдЧрд╡рд╛рддреНрдордХрд╕реНрдп рдкрд╢реНрд╡рдГ рдкрд╢реЛрдГ рдкрд╢реВрдирд╛рдореН ред рдЬрд╛рддрд╛рд╡реЗрдХрд╡рдЪрдирдореН ред рдЪрддреБрдГрд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рдВ рдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд┐ рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдЧреНрд░рднреАрд╖реНрдо рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдЧреГрд╣реАрддрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реНрдордГ ред рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрдЬреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрдЮреНрдЬрдирд╛рд░реНрдердВ рддрдкреНрддрдГ рд╕рдВрддрдкреНрддрдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирд╡рд░реНрдгрдГ рдШрд░реНрдорд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддреН рдорд╣рд╛рд╡реАрд░ рдЗрд╡ рдЕрдпрд╕реНрдордпрдГ рдЕрдпреЛрдордпреЛ рд╣рд┐рд░рдгреНрдордпрдГ рдпрдГ рдХрд▓рд╢рдГ рдЖрд╕реАрддреН рдЕрднрд╡рддреН ‘рддрдореБ рджреЛрд╣рдирд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдХрд▓рд╢рдВ рдЪ рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдГ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдиреЛ рд╡рдпрдВ рд░реБрд╢рдореЗрд╖реБ рдЖрджрд╛рдо рдЖрджрддреНрддрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рее рее реирео рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe have accepted, Agni, the four thousand cattle from the Ru┼Ыam─Бs; and the glowing, the golden ewer prepared for the solemnity, we who are wise have accepted it.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The golden ewer: gharmas’ cit taptaс╕е pravс╣Ыje ya ─Бsid ayasmayaс╕е: ayasmayaс╕е = made of metal, here, made of gold, hiraс╣Зyamaya kala┼Ыa, a ewer;

Gharma┼Ыcit = mah─Бv─лra iva, that is, like the ewer or vessel so termed, containing a mixture of Soma, melted butter, and milk, perhaps put upon the fire: yad ghara ityatapat tad gharmasya gharmatvam it ┼Ыruti

Jamison Brereton

Four thousand bovine livestock have we accepted from the Ru┼Ыamas. Also the gharma pot, which was heated for the Pravargya rite, the one made of copper, that too have we inspired poets taken.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The idiom ─Б╠БтИЪd─Б тАШtakeтАЩ is ordinarily in the middle, whereas ─Б╠Бd─Бma here is active. I consider this active form a secondary formation based on the (pseudo- )active ─Б╠Бdat тАШtookтАЩ, for which see comm. ad V.32.8.

Griffith

We have received four thousand head of cattle presented by the Rusamas, O Agni.
And we, the singers, have received the caldron of metal which was heated for Pravargya.

Geldner

Viertausend St├╝ck Rindvieh haben wir von den Rusama┬┤s empfangen, o Agni. Auch den eisernen Kessel, der zum Sieden der Pravargyamilch erhitzt wurde, haben wir Redekundigen mitbekommen.

Grassmann

Ja viermal tausend Vieh der Rinderheerde empfingen wir von Ru├зamern, o Agni, Und erzgemachten Kessel, ihn zu w├дrmen am Feuer, den erhielten wir, die S├дuger.
